3/4/17, 3:52 AM - Mohammad Ali Butt: ğŸ‘€ AsSalaamOAlaikum all, below is message from Principal Mr. AbdulQuddus Saggo of our beloved school *SKBZAPS*

-------
The Alumni Chipped In Just When It Was Needed 

SKBZAPS had its Irtiqa'a School Inspection from 20th February 2017 to 23rd February 2017. Parallel to ADEC's Irtiqa'a Inspection, the OSHAD i.e. Occupational Safety and Health inspection was also taking place. Both these inspections were extremely crucial this time because the existence and survival of the school was at stake. 

The almost dilapidated condition of various parts of the school building and its failing water supply system are a crystal clear evidence of the negligence of those individuals or bodies that were responsible for the school's good upkeep and maintenance, no matter what claims are made by them.

Schools need to be loved and respected just as a person who loves and maintains his car finds that it lives longer and remains healthier. Similarly, if well brought up grown-ups love, respect and look after after their aging parents, the parents stay healthy and happy.  So, the living and the non-living both need loving care for good health and longevity. Lip service only doesnâ€™t move the needle.


The failures of school water supply system were an embarrassment on normal working days but could be FATAL during the OSHAD Inspection. That's where the Alumni chipped in and donated two brand new pumps with automatic control panels to replace the unreliable makeshift water pumping system.

The school  owes the founding office bearers of the Alumni Association a huge debt of gratitude for their timely contribution towards the health of their aging Alma Mater. 

It's an incontrovertible fact that nobody cares more than the old students for their Alma Mater. The faculty and the Principal  are doing their best to upgrade the basic function of the school i. e. teaching and learning. But more hands and resources are required to bring our school up to par. 

Our next infrastructural challenges are the provision of quality waterproofing of the school roof, renovation of all toilets along with toilets for the handicapped, removing sharp edges and providing slopes, the big ticket challenge of installing a lift for the SEN students, provision of more interactive smart boards, and greening of the football ground of the school.

Looking forward to the good days ahead for the school, about which there is not a sliver of doubt in my mind, because of the founding of the  Alumni Association.

Principal 
SKBZAPS 
Abdul Qudus Saggu                     dated: 3rd March 2017

Dear Faculty Members, I bow down my head in gratitude to Almighty Allah that He has blessed us with this resounding success. We just haven't crept into B band, we are all over it.

The biggest credit goes to faculty. I had belief in you, belief in my students and belief in myself. But we received support from everyone. We ticked all the 6 standards and we could not get a B in PS 6 without the Chairman's orders to immediately repair the damaged part of the building. This time maximum number of Trustees came to see the inspectors to show their support for the school.

The Alumni also chipped in with contribution of two pumps to improve our water supply system. Parents also volunteered to help where their help was required . So, almost everyone played their part in this success. 

Quality education is a team sport. No one, howsoever brilliant or outstanding he may be, can do it alone. Good schools have collaborative culture and its the collective input of all that produces good results and quality. But no doubt, the greatest credit goes to the Faculty of Sheikh Khalifa School. 

This is just the beginning but a great beginning. The journey is long and we have to reinforce the good practices that we have established. Today I was in Dubai, attending a symposium of about one thousand Principals from across the UAE when I got this wonderful news. I am very proud of you all. Well done and keep it up!

3/16/17, 12:27 AM - Atif Saeed HS: This is how Business competitors are seen in Saudi Arabia.
A brother moved to Makkah many years ago. He was a high flying manager of major departmental stores in U.K., Malaysia and China. He had been brought in by Bin Dawood stores as a regional manager for the Makkah region. He was from England. 

After living and working in Saudi for some time, he later narrated how he found it so strange, unique and uplifting in how business was done in Saudi. Here were the examples he gave:

1. In Makkah, next to a major Bin Dawood superstore a rival new company were entering the kingdom and decided to open a mega store right next to Bin Dawood, within metres. The brother was perturbed, "Why can't they open just somewhere else."The owners of Bin Dawood frowned on his outlook. They ordered him to send his workers to the other store being setup and offer them tea and food and any help they needed to setup! The brother was left  astounded. The Bin Dawood management simply replied, "Our rizq is fixed, they cannot take even a single riyal from what has been decreed upon us. So why not gain ajr and help them." 

2. The owner of alFakieh poultry in Saudi, he has a famous mosque in MAKKAH (Masjid Faqih). He is very rich Ù…Ø§Ø´Ø§Ø¡ Ø§Ù„Ù„Ù‡ ØªØ¨Ø§Ø±Ùƒ Ø§Ù„Ù„Ù‡ and religious. He found out that his major rival AlWatania was floundering with huge debts of a million plus riyals. So he one day sent a cheque to the owner of AlWatania and said, "Pay off your debt, and pay me back, whenever you can." He had the opportunity to become the sole major distributor of chicken but instead he decided to help his main rival.

3/29/17, 10:18 PM - IMRAN SOHAIL HS: Life in the army they say is mighty fine....

Army officers are the most amazingly easy people to get along with. Should you fall in love with one and decide to marry him, here is what you can expect.

1. He will be extremely respectful to your parents and your family. He may not understand why your brother has long hair or sleeps late, but he will try to understand...because he loves you. However, there will be indirect hints about getting up at 0500 hrs (it's never 5 am) and doing 5 km with 100 push ups. And how a crew cut is the most fashionable hairstyle ever.

2. Going to a party is a parade. 2000 hrs means 1955 hrs. Right time, right kit (dress) and right place.

3. Your husband may be a young captain but when you enter a room, all officers will get up to wish you...and that includes Generals too. That is the level of respect you can expect...every time.

4. If he is out for work and you are alone, expect EXTRA attention from the Unit ladies. You didn't marry just him...you married the army.

5. He will be extremely loving and understanding, but you have to understand that to him "Roger" is as romantic as "Yes, honey".

6. Expect Young Officers (YOs) to land up at your house at odd hours demanding food. It won't happen frequently, but by God it will happen. Scrambled eggs are acceptable food. The youngsters will offer to help. Decline gracefully. Army YOs are like good natured rhinos in a bone china shop.

8. When he meets your school and college friends, he will very polite with the ladies. He will open doors and pull chairs. Chivalry is in his DNA. He is NOT flirting. That's just the way he has been trained.

9. He is not walking on your left hand side. He is 9 o'clock to you. The building is not in front...its 12 o'clock. 

10. He will eat rice with a fork, unless it's a sit down dinner. If it's rotis he is eating, he will use the fork to push the dal or veggie to the roti. That's just how all officers eat. 

11. He will eat at a dhaba if you so desire, but will maintain fauji table manners. He will "open" and "close" his plate. If he uses a toothpick, he will cover his mouth with the other hand.

12. He will drink but never get drunk. His manners will always be impeccable.

13. Guderian, Rommel and Clausewitz are not his coursemates. 

14. If he is with his coursemates, don't expect him to behave his age. They are the only competition you have in terms of attention.

15. He does not want to know what happened at the Ladies Club. Poor man has suffered enough. 

16. He will respect you for being strong. And he will be happy for you to take centerstage, with him cheering you from the sidelines....goofy grin and all.

17. Though it depends on the ethnicity of the troops that he commands, don't be surprised if you are called "Sir" sometimes. No disrespect is meant. 

18. He is probably the most secure man you have ever seen. He will have very little self doubt. All the ribbons that he wears on his chest are the reason.

19. He will never use foul language in the presence of ladies. This is not to say that his "grammar" is not up to the mark. On the contrary, he probably has a PhD in "language". But NEVER in the presence of ladies. 

20. While he will have enough for you to be comfortable, he is never going to be rich. But if you count your wealth in an extended family of a million warriors, tons of love, respect and loyalty...well ma'am you have married a guy richer than Bill Gates.

If he is alone in a room and looking happy, it's just him admiring his Raybans ğŸ˜€
